3.23            The Bank's country-specific, standard bidding documents of June 1994 will be used for
ICB procurement. The laws and regulations governing local procurement procedures and practices in



-32-
Romania are being reviewed, and it is expected that the Country Procurement Assessment Report will
be completed this fiscal year. The findings of that review will be discussed with the Romanian
authorities and agreements wIll be sought regarding any changes needed to make the procedures
acceptable to the Bank.
3.24        All equipment and materials to be financed from the Bank loan proceeds will be
procured in accordance with the Guidelnes for Procuranent under IBRD Loans and IDA
Credits' (May 1992). Romanian suppliers competing for contracts for the supply of goods procured
under ICB procedures will receive a preference in bid evaluation of 15% of the CEP price or the
prevailing customs duty applicable to non-exempt importers, whichever is less, provided it can be
proved that the value added to the product in Romania exceeds 20% of the ex-factory bid price.
3.25        The dvil works included under the project consist of the rehabilitation of offices (about
170 building sites in 41 judets with an average rehabilitation cost of about US$30,000, excluding
contingencies and taxes), facilities for RATCs, and construction of new labor offices. All costs
related to civil works will be financed by the Government (US$ 11.0 million) according to local
procedures.
3.26        The goods to be financed from the Bank loan proceeds include equipment and
materials, computer hardware and software, and vehicles. Contracts for goods estimated to cost more
than US$300,000 equivalent each will be procured through ICB. To the extent practical, equipment
and materials will be grouped into about 12 packages of sizes that will interest large segments of
international vendors. Computers will be grouped into about three major packages (total value
estimated US$10.6 million). Contracts for goods (including supplies - para. 3.28) estimated to cost
the equivalent of US$300,000 or less, up to an aggregate of US$7.0 million, may be awarded on the
basis of price quotations from at least three suppliers from at least three eligible source countries.
Items that cannot be grouped or groups of items estimated to cost less than the equivalent of
US$50,000 per contract, or off-the-shelf items, up to an aggregate amount not to exceed
US$3.0 million, may be purchased on the basis of a minimum of three price quotations obtained from
qualified suppliers. Contracts for goods which the Bank agrees are of proprietary nature (e.g.,
computer software packages) may be awarded after direct negotiations with suppliers, in accordance
with procedures acceptable to the Bank.
3.27        Consultants for technical assistance (TA) financed under the Bank loan (totalling
US$19.3 million: US$13.9 million for consultancies; US$5.4 million for training)) will be procured
on the basis of a short list of qualified firms and will follow the 'Guidelines for the Use of
Consultants by World Bank Borrowers and by the World Bank as Executing Agency' (August
1981). Chart 3.1 (page 28) shows the nine TA packages to be financed under the loan; and Annexes
10 and 17 provide details on the nine packages and the selection criteria. TORs for these packages
were finalized at negotiations. With respect to training, to the extent possible, selected TA
contractors will also coordinate overseas fellowships and local training, in conjunction with local
firms (see Annex 11 for a detailed summary of fellowships and training).
3.28        The incremental operating costs to be financed under the loan include non-salary
operating costs of investment such as office and administrative supplies and consumables, computer
supplies and consumables, and other costs related to project execution. The Bank will finance an
estimated US$7.6 million equivalent for supplies (an estimated US$4.9 million of which will be
procured on the basis of price quotations from at least three suppliers from three eligible source



-33-
countries, and an estimated US$2.7 million on the basis of a minimum of three price quotations from
qualified suppliers). All other operating costs, including all local salary costs, will be financed by the
Government (US$19.3 million).
3.29        All contracts of a value exceeding US$300,000 equivalent will be subject to the Bank's
prior review. It is expected that about 12 ICB contracts will be subject to this provision. All
consultant contracts (with the exception of small contracts valued at less that US$100,000 - of which
current packaging has foreseen none, although a case for which may arise during implementation),
will be subject to prior review, as will terms of reference for all consulting assignments. Selective
post-review of awarded contracts below the threshold level will be carried out on about one in four
goods equipment and materials contracts. It is expected that local suppliers will participate in all ICB
goods procurement. The PCU will coordinate all procurement activities. To assist the PCU in this
area, a long-term project implementation consultant, as well as short-term procurement experts, will
be hired. Estimated timing of procurement activities over the project life is outlined in Annex 17.
3.30        Procurement information will be collected and recorded as follows: (a) prompt report
of contract award information by the Borrower; and (b) comprehensive quarterly reports to the Bank
by the Borrower (assisted by consultants) indicating (i) revised cost estimates for individual contracts
and the total project, including best estimates of allowances for physical and price contingencies,
(ii) revised timing of procurement actions, including advertising, bidding, contract award, and
completion time for individual contracts, and (iii) compliance with aggregate limits on specified
methods of procurement.
3.31        Disbursements. Disbursements will be made as follows:
(a) 100 percent of foreign expenditures and 100 percent of local expenditures (ex-
factory cost) for equipment and materials, and 80 percent of local expenditures for
other items procured locally;
(b) 100 percent of the expenditures for consulting services;
(c) 100 percent of expenditures for fellowships abroad and local training; and
(d) 100 percent of total expenditures for supplies.
3.32      All disbursements will be fully documented except goods costing less than US$300,000
equivalent, local training, and supply purchases, for which disbursements will be made against
statements of expenditure (SOE), certified by the director of the PCU. The required supporting
documentation will be retained by the PCU for at least one year after receipt by the Bank of the audit
report for the year in which the last disbursement was made. This documentation will be made
available for review by the auditors and by visiting staff upon request. A tentative disbursement
schedule for the loan is presented in Annex 12. The Project closing date will be September 30, 2001.
3.33      Special Account. To facilitate timely project implementation, the Government will
establish, maintain and operate, under terms and conditions acceptable to the Bank, a Special Account
in convertible currency, to which the World Bank will make an initial deposit of US$2.5 million.
The Special Account will be replenished every four months, or whenever one third of the authorized
balance will have been withdrawn. Documentation requirements for replenishment applications will



-34-
follow the procedures required by the Bank disbursement department. In addition, monthly bank
statements of the special account which have been reconciled by the Borrower will accompany all
replenishment requests. A project account in lei wDI be established prior to loan effectiveness and
wIll be used by the PCU for expenditures to be covered by Government financing.
3.34      Proiect Accounts and Audits. The PCU wIll maintain separate accounts for all project
activities, in conformity with international accounting practices. Project accounts, including the
Special Account, wIll be audited in accordance with the Bank 'Guidelines for Financial Reporting and
Auditing of Projects Financed by the World Bank' (March 1982). The Bank will be provided, within
six months of the end of each fiscal year of the Government, an audit report of such scope and detail
as the Bank may reasonably request, including a separate opinion by the auditor on disbursements
against certified SOEs. The separate opinion should mention whether the SOEs submitted during the
fiscal year, together with the procedures and internal controls involved in their preparation, can be
relied upon to support the related withdrawal applications.
E.        Project Reporting and Evaluation
3.35      R nrting. The PCU will prepare semi-annual descriptive and financial reports
(beginning from the date of Loan Effectiveness) on each project component, objective and activity
describing: (a) current status; (b) deviations, if any, from the implementation schedule; and (c)
reasons for deviations and corrective actions being taken. Project monitoring indicators were
developed during appraisal, and sample progress reporting documents are in the POM. Reporting and
Bank supervision will focus on in-depth reviews of the policy framework for sectoral improvements,
the consistency of activities for each component and sub-component with agreements reached at
negotiations, performance of the implementing groups and institutions, assessment of emerging needs
for adjustments to project parameters, and possible follow-up operations which could be supported by
the Bank. The bases of Bank supervision will be the semi-annual progress reports and the annual
evaluation of project activities by MOLSP, supplemented by a review of project expenditures and
availability of financial resources, in addition to substantive discussions with technical assistance
providers assisting in the implementation of various components, and discussions with senior officials
of the MOLSP and the Ministry of Finance. The POM, finalized and agreed upon with the
Government during Negotiations, will also be used to assist supervision and reporting. During
negotiations, the Government provided assurances that it will review sectoral reform progress
annually with the Bank according to an agreed set of monitoring indicators and prepare jointly with
the Bank a mid-term review of project execution to verify that the project components are operating
according to the agreed criteria and procedures and to incorporate modifications where necessary (no
later than June 30, 1997).
3.36      Mid-Term Review/Evaluation. The Govermnent and project authorities will prepare a
mid-term report of project execution about two years after loan effectiveness, and no later than June
30, 1997. The annual work program for the year following the joint mid-term review will need to
reflect the recommendations of the review. The project completion date will be March 31, 2001.

and the bidding process launched.

IV. BENEFTrS AND RISKS
A.       Ben
4.1       The project will significantly assist in the restructuring of the economy by strengthening
the capacity to cope with unemployment, improving labor mobility, and providing the new skills
needed in a market economy for both workers and managers. Upon completion of the project,
Romania will have in place an employment service and job training system which will quicldy
respond to shifting market needs. The MOLSP will improve its organization and management
capabilities through the automation and project monitoring to be put into place. The social safety net,
which the project will help build up, will strengthen the political will needed to pursue economic
reforms during the period when poverty and other social problems intensify. These benefits from the
social safety net are not just of a humanitarian nature but, as demonstrated by the experience of
OECD countries, represent a significant investment in human resources and contribute to financial
savings by avoiding more serious problems resulting from neglect of pressing social needs.
B.       Risks
4.2       A major risk to successful implementation of the project is that of present implementation
capacity of the MOLSP is insufficiently developed relative to the complexity of the tasks of building
up both reactive and proactive employment and social protection programs. Although MOLSP has
now acquired implementation experience in the smaller-scale TACI Project, this much larger project
will require strengthening the implementation capacity of the MOLSP. The implementation plan
incorporates lessons learned in the TACI Project, and appropriate and sufficient amounts of TA and
training, focusing on helping the MOLSP make the transition to large-scale project management. A
project supervision plan has been formulated to assist the MOLSP in following Bank guidelines by
helping in the preparation of standard bidding and contract documents. Nonetheless, intense
supervision from headquarters and the resident mission will be required to minimize the risks posed
by weak implementation capacity.
4.3       A second important risk to successful implementation of the project is that of adequate
financing for the incremental recurrent costs, especially for additional staffing required under the
Employment Services Component. This has been a problem in other countries in the region,
especially as unemployment rises sharply and Government budgets become increasingly constrained,
where additional staff budgets are not allocated to increase and improve the quality of services. This
risk is being addressed by explicitly highlighting the need for incremental staffing, including it in the
project cost estimates, and securing the commitment of both the Ministry of Finance and the MOLSP
to adequate staffing levels.

INSTITUTIONAL DZSCRIPTION OF TRZ CASH BZNIFIT SYSTeM l
UNEMPLOYMENT -BENEFIT
The unemployment was not officially recognized (for political reasons)
during the previous regime. Beginning with 1991 the unemployment was
officially recognized and the unemployment benefits were introduced. The level
of unemployment increased rapidly from 3.1 percent in 1991 to 8.4 percent in
1992 and 10.2 by the end of 1993. The latest estimate in February 1994 was
11.3 percent. The unemployment benefits are paid out of the unemployment fund
which is founded from contributions of both the employers (5 percent on the
total wage bill) and employees (1 percent on their individual wage bill).
Benefit levels. The size of unemployment benefit varies from 50 percent
to 60 percent of the wage in the final three months in the last job (depending
upon the length of service) or from 75 percent to 85 percent of the minimum
wage if the last wage was below minimum wage. The benefit formula is shown in
Table 1.
Duration of benefit. The duration of benefit is 270 days. After the
completion of 270 days the unemployed people are entitled to a post-
unemployment support benefit which is 40 percent of the minimum wage, for a
period of 18 months.
Eligibility rules. At present eligibility for unemployment benefit
extends to anyone over 19 years old who is unemployed due to liquidation or
shrinkage of a firm. Those with enough agricultural land to support themselves
are excluded. Unemployed school leavers from poor families (excluded in most
countries) are eligible.
Withholding benefit: refusal of job/training offers: an individual who
refuses two 'reasonable' offers will lose benefit. A 'reasonable' offer can
be either an appropriate job or an appropriate training course. If a Labor
Office whose offer of training has been refused then fails to find the
individual a job and a further offer of training is refused, it can cut off
benefit. Failure to keep in touch with the Labor Office will lead to the
benefit cancellation. Failure to declare a job placement will be penalized.
Utrating of benefit A result of inflation, the unemployment benefits are
periodically indexed, together with the wages and other social safety
benefits.
Related benefits
School leavers nroqwrams. In addition to the unemployment benefit scheme,
the MOLSP has attempted three other measures to help the unemployed. The first
is a wage subsidy program for secondary school and university graduates. In
this scheme, initiated for the 1992 graduates ant then extended yearly,
participating firms receive a wage subsidy equal to the-graduate entitlement
This annex was prepared by Nichoas Barr for th red cover report, Romanit Human Resources and the
Transion to a Market Economy (1992). Sorne of the nfrmation has been updaed by Richard Flores
(ECIRO).



43
Annex I
Page 3 of 17
to the unemployment benefit. The success of this program has been very limited
and it is not clear that even that disappointing results are, in fact, due to
the wage subsidy program.
Training Droqrams. The second measure is the training for unemployed.
The labour offices arrange retraining courses with a variety of institutions,
but the completion rate and the job placement rates are very low. A large part
of the lack of success is due to lack of time and proper training on the part
of staff to screen and council potential trainees, conduct proper labor market
analysis and to make and follow up on contracts with employers. In addition
the institutions supplying the training are the traditional vocational
schools, which are not used to providing training in a market oriented
environment. Problems with the training programs are also due to lack of
vacancies from the weak labour demand.
Small business Droc'rams. The third measure is a program to promote small
business start-ups by the unemployed by providing training in business skills.
This has been the least successful, not surprisingly, because it is the most
difficult program among the three measures.
Unemnlovment Fund
In spite of the continuous increase of the unemployment, the
unemployment fund registered important surplus amounted to 1 percent of the
GDP only for 1993. The surplus comes from the relatively high tax (which was
imposed prior the effectiveness of the unemployment benefits) and the gradual
increases in unemployment. While it is true that the accumulated surplus is
substantial, its real value is being eroded by inflation. However, the
surpluses could turn into deficits in the next years, as the tax base, and
hence revenues, decline due to reductions in salaried employment, and as
expenditures increase due to increases in eligible unemployment. In case the
unemployment fund will face a deficit, the State Budget will make it up.
Administration
The administration of unemployment benefit scheme is carried out through
the local offices of the MOLSP. The labor offices are presently overwhelmed
with claims processing and can barely provide good job assistance and
retraining services, such as counseling workers on job search strategies and
opportunities for training.
SOCIAL INSUR-ANCE
Social insurance has widespread coverage in Romania. It includes
essentially universal entitlement to old age, disability, and survivors,
pensions as well as sick and maternity leave. Among all the social insurance
instruments the pensions are the most important ones, in terms of coverage and
expenditures (7.5 percent from the GDP in 1993).



44
Annex l
Page 4 of 17
The system has been complicated by the existence multiple social
insurance funds (almost 10 independent schemes). Starting with mid 1933, these
funds have been unified and reduced in number such as: (a) the main state
fund, which covers employees in the state and private sectors and self-
employed individuals; (b) the agricultural fund; and (c) other two independent
funds, including one each for lawyers, and clergy. Each of these funds has two
components: the main fund, and the supplementary pensions fund. Assessments of
the status of the first two largest social insurance schemes are presented
here.
I.    CONTRIBUTIONS
The State Social Insurance Fund
Social insurance contributions and benefits hitherto were consolidated
with the general government budget. From 1991 the Social Insurance Fund has
been separated from the main central government budget.
The main benefits funded by the state Social Insurance Fund are
(a) sickness benefits, (b) maternity benefits, and (c) the main social
insurance pensions for (i) employees in the state and private sectors, and
(ii) self-employed individuals with a contributions record.
Contributions to the main state scheme:
(a)   Prior to November 1990 the normal contribution for employees was:
state and private sectors, 14 percent of the enterprise wage
bill; government sector (ministries, schools, hospitals, etc.),
13 percent; state agriculture, nine percent; household
employees, seven percent; joint ventures with overseas companies,
25 percent. Self-employed individuals paid a 14 percent
contribution on a voluntary basis. Since wages are difficult to
determine for a self-employed person, such people pay a
contribution based on a deemed wage equal to that of a director of
a medium size state enterprise.
(b)   Since November 1990 the State Social Insurance Fund has been based
on mandatory contributions paid mainly by the state owned and
private companies amounted to 25 percent of the payroll. The self-
employed pay the same contribution based o8 an income statement on
voluntary basis. The rationale for the change is to attempt to put
the autonomous Social Insurance Fund onto a sound financial
footing.
Budget balance: any deficit on the Social Insurance Fund will be made
up from the government budget. Liberalization of the early-retirement
provisions (see the discussion of pensions, below) resulted in a substantial
deficit of the Social Insurance Fund in 1990. Enforcement of the contribution
in the emerging private sector was difficult. Early retirement and the-
enforcement problem, together with the separation of the main Social Insurance



45
Annex I
Page 5 of 17
Fund from the central government budget, motivated the contribution increase.
The State Sunolementary Pensions Fund
In the past, workers paid a two percent contribution towards a
supplementary pension;  they also had the option of paying a further,
voluntary two percent contribution, making four percent in all. Since 1986
the voluntary contribution has been abolished, and workers pay a contribution
of three percent of their basic wage (i.e. net of bonuses and overtime) to pay
for their supplementary pension (described below). The supplementary pension
contribution for self-employed workers is voluntary.
These contributions flow into the state Supplementary Pensions Fund,
from which Supplementary Pensions are paid.
The Social Insurance Fund for Farmers
The second largest pension fund is the Agricultural Pension Fund;it
covers 1.3 mil. pensioners (almost 29 percent of the total number of
pensioners in 1993). Prior 1991, its revenues derived from three main sources:
(a)   Contributions in respect of members of agricultural co-operatives,
of 9.5 percent no of the co-operative's total wage bill but of
the total value of its sales, i.e. the tax base is not wages but
turnover.
(b)   A transfer from the central government budget of two percent of
the value of agricultural co-operative sales to the state sector.
(c)   Contributions from inter co-operative associations (e.g. an
association of poultry breeders) (4.5 percent of total sales).
Since 1990, when the agricultural co-operatives have been abolished the
scheme was run with big deficits. This deficits were covered by loans form
state insurance fund or by subsidies from the state budget. According to the
new legislation the financing is based on:
(a)   voluntary contributions of the private farmers (7 percent over the
monthly insured income).
(b)   mandatory contributions of the companies which are producing,
processing or trading agro-products (2-4 percent over their
revenues after the deduction of taxes).
As a first step towards establishment of a unified pension system,
starting with 1993 the Agriculture Pension Scheme was taken over by the MOLSP
which currently administrates it.
The fund pays broadly the same range of benefits (though generally at a
lower level) as derive from the main social insurance fund.
II.   BENEFITS



46
Annex I
Page 6 of 17
Sickness Benefit
Eligibility rules: coverage includes workers in all sectors including
the state sector, the private sector, self-employed individuals (so long as
contributions have been paid). Benefit is payable to members of the labor
force who are either ill themselves or who are unable to work because they
live in an area which has been quarantined. The major exclusion is workers in
private agriculture.
Benefit levels: Benefits under the main scheme depend on whether or not
the illness/injury is work-related. Where it is not, benefit is dependent (a)
on previous earnings, and (b) upon length of time in the labor force, as shown
in Table 2. Where the illness/injury is work-related, benefit is 85 percent
of previous earnings, irrespective of duration in the labor force. Until
1990, members of agricultural co-operatives received sickness benefit at a
lower rate. Since January 1, 1990 benefits have been the same as for members
of the state scheme.
Duration of benefit is normally up to 180 days. If there is no prospect
of recovery thereafter, the individual transfers to a disability pension.
Exenditure and numbers of recilpients of sicmess benefit are set out in
Tables 6 and 7. In 1989, sickness benefit at an average daily rate of Lei 91
was paid in respect of 45 million days of sick leave, an average of 5.6 days
per worker. Total expenditure on sickness benefit in 1989 was Lei 4.1 billion.
Administration of Sickness Benefit
Sickness benefit is administered by the enterprise. Benefit is paid by
the enterprise on the basis of certification by an enterprise-based doctor or
by policlinic/hospital doctor. When an enterprise has paid sickness benefit,
it recovers the money by withdrawing it from the bank account in which it has
deposited its social insurance contributions. Beginning with 1990 granting of
sick leave benefits became more relaxed. As a result of this, sick leave
claims increased by almost 50 percent. this had an important impact on the
social insurance fund which covered entirely the sick leave costs. Many abuses
have been noticed.
The legislation was modified in 1992, when it was decided that first 10
days of the sick leave be covered by the employer and the rest by the
insurance fund.
Related Sickness Benefits.
PeolDe iniured during the revolution are entitled to sickness benefit at
100 percent of their previous wage with no limit as to duration.
Maternity Benefit



47
Annex 1
Page 7 of 17
Eliaibility rules: coverage applies to mothers who at the time they
became pregnant were working in the state sector, the private sector, or
agricultural sector.
Benefit levels. First and second children: benefit is 50 percent of
the mother's previous wage if she has been in the labor force for less than
six months; 65 percent if she has been in the labor force 6-12 months, and 85
percent if over 12 months. Third and subsequent children: 94 percent of
previous wage irrespective of time in the labor force. Since January 1, 1990
benefits have been the same as for members of the state insurance scheme.
Duration of benefit is 112 calendar days, 52 before the birth and 60
afterwards. Women cannot be dismissed whilst in receipt of maternity benefit.
Related Maternity Benefits.
Short-time working durina Dreqnancv: for the last three months before
taking maternity leave a woman is entitled to work for only six hours per day
with no loss of pay; the wage differential is paid out of the Social
Insurance Fund.
Mothers with sick children: a woman who has to stay at home to look
after a sick child under three years old is entitled to benefit at the same
rate as maternity benefit.
Mothers with a child under one Year old: under a new law passed in
February 1990, a mother with a child under one year old may stay at home on 65
percent of her previous wage.
Expenditure and numbers of recipients are set out in Tables 6 and 7.
Benefit at an average rate of Lei 76.7 per day was paid to 34,000 women
entitled either to maternity leave or who were at home looking after a sick
child. Total expenditure in 1989 was Lei 2.6 billion.
Administration of Maternity Benefits
Maternity and related benefits are administered by the enterprise in
broadly the same way as sickness benefit.
Pensions
The structure of pensions is threefold: social insurance pensions;
supplementary pensions; and various other pensions. Social insurance
pensions are of three sorts, relating to retirement, invalidity and survivors'
benefits, respectively. The supplementary retirement pension is additional to
the national insurance pension and is paid for by an additional contribution.
The third group comprises a variety of other social insurance pensions: for
Second World War veterans; for people with only between five and 10 years in
the labor force; for workers in agricultural co-operatives; and for workers
in private (mainly peasant) agriculture.    -



48
Annex 1
Page 8 of 17
Social Insurance Pensions (Retirement)
Eliqibilitv rules. (1) Pensionable age: though the normal retirement
age is 60 (55 women), there has been considerable erosion. There are three
groups for retirement purposes: Group 1 includes heavy and/or dangerous work,
e.g. mining, chemistry, oil exploration, steel workers, anyone involved in the
flying side of aviation, opera singers and ballerinas: individuals may retire
at age 50 (men and women), provided that they have worked for at least 20
years. Group 2 includes not as heavy/dangerous as group 1: individuals may
retire at age 55 (50 in the case of women), provided that they have worked for
at least 25 years (20 women). Group 3 is the theoretical norm: individuals
may retire at age 60 (55 in the case of women), provided that they have worked
for at least 30 years (25 women).
Prior to 1990 about 10 percent of workers were in groups 1 and 2. The
definition of who qualified tended to be generous. For instance, the early-
retirement entitlement of workers in petrol refineries was extended to
everyone in the refinery industry, including clerical staff, etc.
In 1990, Decree 60 allowed workers in all three groups to retire five
years earlier than previously. The Decree, which led to a wave of early
retirement (at a very rough estimate, about 800,000), was in force until
January 1991. This wave of early retirement was the main cause of a deficit
of the Social Insurance Fund in 1990 of Lei S billion.
Eligibility rules. (2) Retirement conditions: under certain
circumstances it is possible to receive a pension and continue to work, at
least part time.
(a)   It is possible to work after retirement provided that the sum of
the pension and post-retirement earnings do not exceed the pre-
retirement wage. If earnings x pension exceed the previous wage,
the pension is reduced Leu for Leu with the excess over the
previous wage.
(b)   Notwithstanding (a), workers in certain key industries may work
for up to three months in the year without any loss of pension,
however high their earnings during those three months. Though
hard data were not available, a rough estimate is that such
workers amount to some 10 percent of the labor force.
(c)   Notwithstanding (a), self-employed retirees, workers in co-
operative farms and in private agriculture do not lose any pension
if they continue to work.
Benefit levels: the level of the social insurance pension depends (a)
on the level of previous warnings of the last five years, (b) upon the
worker's group (as defined above), and (c) upon years of work. Details of the
full pension (i.e. where a person has worked for the requisite number of
years) are set out in Table 3. Workers in the first two groups (i.e. those
who are allowed to retire early) receive a higher pension, other things being
equal, than individuals in the third group.  Where-a-person-works for more-
than the required number of years, he/she receives an additional one percent



49
Annex I
Page 9 of 17
of pension for each extra year for the first five extra years, and an
additional 0.5 percent per year thereafter.
Unratinc of benefit: there was no formal requirement that pensions be
uprated in line with inflation. In practice, pension levels are reviewed from
time to time (1977, 1979, 1982, 1984, 1988). The resulting increases did not
always fully account for inflation; higher pensions are sometimes increased
proportionately less than lower ones.
Since the indexation of wages and other incomes became a common
practice, the pensions are periodically adjusted through Government Decisions.
Generally the indexation formulas have been forward looking with coefficients
below expected inflation. In addition the Government has declared ad hoc
fixed-sum compensations as reimbursement for the raising of food prices.
Related Pensions
The SuzDlementary Pension: the contribution conditions were described
above. They buy an additional pension which is shown in Table 3B. The
pension is not uprated.
Retirement Densions for other aroups: Benefits under the main social
insurance scheme: (a) Pensions for Second World War veterans, (b) pensions
for individuals with only 5-10 years in the labor force are paid at a fixed
level of Lei 700/month. Pensions for workers in agricultural co-operatives:
the following are the main differences from the state scheme: (a)
contributions (which are lower than for the main state scheme) are paid into a
different fund, (b) the normal retirement age is 65 (60 women), (c) the
pension is lower than in the main state scheme. The pension is related to the
number of contribution years and to the income of the co-operative. Reform
during 1990 established a minimum pension of Lei 500 and a maximum of Lei 1300
per month, with an average of about Lei 650/month, (d) a Draft Law seeks to
lower the retirement age to 60 (55 women) and to pay pensions for members of
agricultural co-operatives according to the same formula as under the main
social insurance scheme, (c) pensions for workers in private (mainly peasant)
agriculture: reform during 1990 established a minimum pension of Lei
500/month to a maximum of Lei 1300/month.
Social Insurance Pensions (Invalidity)
Eligibility rules. The definition of disability is common between the
MOLSP and the Ministry of Health: there are three degrees of disability: (a)
First degree: no autonomy; (b) Second degree: some autonomy, but cannot
work; (c) Third degree: less than 50 percent work capacity. There is a
disability commission in each district which determines the degree of
invalidity of applicants.
Benefit levels are based on the formula for the retirement pension (see
Table 3): (a) First degree: 100 percent of the retirement pension + Lei
300/month ,  (b) - Sec0cd degree: tS percent- of the- retirement-pension,- -tc) Third
degree: 60 percent of the retirement pension; the pension is unaffected by



50
Annex 1
Page 10 of 17
any earnings the individual has.
Duration of benefit: Benefit normally commences after a person has
received sick pay for 180 days. Eligibility is checked every six months to a
year; benefit is payable so long as the disability persists.
Social Insurance Pensions (Widows)
A widow living alone and aged 55 or more is entitled to either her own
pension or a widow's pensions, whichever is the larger. The widow's pension
is equal to half of her deceased husband's pension; a widow with one child
receives 75 percent of the pension; a widow with three or more children
receives the whole pension. Where a widow is under 55, she receives the
pension just described for six months only. The definition of children for
the purposes of widow's pension is a child under 16, or under 25 if in full-
time education.
Administration of Social Insurance Pensions
The administration of the main social insurance pension and the
supplementary pension is integrated.
The Ministry of Labor in Bucharest has computerized contribution
records. Each month it prints a list of all pensioners (name, address, amount
of pension to be paid), which it sends to the post office in each District.
The District post office staggers mailings. On the appointed day each
month, it sends each pensioner a envelope containing (a) his/her pension in
cash, and (b) a statement of the amount of the pension, including a tear-off
slip which the pensioner signs and returns to the postman. Alternatively, the
pensioner has the option of asking the post office to deposit the pension
directly into his/her bank account.
Reform issues
A White Paper prepared by the MOLSP, sets out the options and the major
proposals to be considered for a new further pension law. These proposals are
listed below:
- An unified public pension system that will integrate all the
independent systems is needed. Administrative responsibility for the
system should be transferred to a new independent agency, that would
report to the MOLSP.
- A new benefits structure for social insurance and pensions is
recommended.
- A gradually increase of the retirement age is envisaged in order to
ensure -the future solvency of- the pension fund. The- income -to --be used
in determining social insurance contributions, pensions, and other



51
Annex I
Page 11 of 17
benefits be clearly defined.
- A simplified pension calculation formula is proposed in order to
increase the system's transparency and fairness, and to improve
distribution within and between generations.
- In evaluating social insurance contributions, it is suggested that
responsibility for contributions for employed persons be allocated
between employers and employees, in proportions that would differ
among work groups.
- A strategy for developing a voluntary private pension scheeme is laid
out to complement the public pension system. Such a private scheeme
would allow people to add substantially to their retirement incomes.
SOCIAL ASSISTANCE
Family Allowance
During the previous regime, the cash payments as well as the tax credits
were provided both to ensure support to the families with children, and to
stimulate the natality. This section describes the family benefits as of
October 1990, as well as the provisions of the new legal framework.
Elicibilitvy rules. Until 1993 when the new legislation was approved,
system covered: (a) children of employees of state enterprises: the father
receives the family allowance via the enterprise (the money derives from the
central government budget; the enterprise merely administers payment). If
the father is not employed in the state sector but the mother is, the payment
is made to the mother; (b) Employees of agricultural and other co-operatives
receive their family allowance from the co-operative. In the case of non-
agricultural co-operatives, such allowances derive from the co-operative's
income, not from the central government budget. The children of: self-
employed individuals, employees in the private sector, unemployed or non-
employed people, and of workers in private agriculture were excluded.
The newly approved legislation (end of 1993) extended the coverage area
of the child allowance to all resident children in Romania (no matter the
citizenship). At the same time the tax credits have been removed. The child
allowances are currently administrated by: (a) MOLSP for the pre-school age
children and (b) Ministry of Education for school age children.
Benefit levels as they are shown in Table 4. were differentiated based
on the wage and number of children. In the case of members of agricultural co-
operatives, family allowances are paid at the lowest of the three levels in
the Table.
According to the new legislation the allowance became a fixed-sum which
is not related to the number of children or family income. The child allowance



52
Annex 1
Page 12 of 17
is uprated periodically together with the wages and other incomes.
Duration of benefit: current law: till age 16 (if handicapped till age
18). Handicapped individuals receive the Lei 1000/month described above for
the duration of the handicap, if necessary for life.
The new law establish the benefit duration till the age of 16 or till 18
in full time education.
Related Family Benefits
Maternity pension: a mother with three or more children receives an
additional allowance of Lei 400/month (3 children) or Lei 500/month (4 or more
children). The benefit is payable to the mother for life, i.e. it is a
maternity pension.
Birth allowance: under current arrangements there is a one-time payment
for each birth after the first of Lei 1500.
Wives of conscripts: the pregnant wife of a military conscript receives
a payment of Lei 500/month (Lei 300/month in villages), provided that she
conforms with various conditions.
Guardian's Allowance: foster parents receive Lei 1000/month/child they
look after. The payment was raised from its previous level of Lei 400 in a
Law passed in February 1990.
Administration
Current arrangements: administration of the main family allowance is
through the MOLSP and Ministry of Education. Maternity pension is
administered at the Primaria level by the same team that administers social
assistance. Payment is to the mother at her enterprise if she works. If she
does not work, she can be paid at the enterprise where her husband works if
she goes there in person, or (as with the main pensions) she can be paid by
post. The birth allowance is also administered by the Primaria team, normally
through the post.
Other benefits
With the exception of six centrally-funded social assistance residential
institutions for the elderly, and two special schools run by non-profit
organizations, all social assistance is funded out of the local (District)
budget. Importantly, however, there is provision for central assistance if a
District overspends its social assistance budget in the face of higher-than-
expected demands on it.
Benefits for Handicapped Peolle.
Eligibility rules:  Under the Law of February 1990 the person must be:



53
Annex I
Page 13 of 17
over 16; handicapped in he first, second or third degree, as defined for
invalidity pension (in the previous law, people handicapped in the third
degree had to work); have no income; have no relatives (defined as parents or
children) with wages (i.e. net of family allowance, etc.) higher than Lei
1000/month/person in the family.
Benefit levels: individuals who meet the qualifying conditions receive
a cash benefit of Lei 500/month plus, where relevant, free prostheses.
Duration of benefit is without limit.
Related Benefits
Death or nermanent handicap during the revolution: Death during
revolution: the surviving family,receives a one-time payment of Lei 1500.
Permanent handicap: one-off payments of: Lei 20,000 if a person is an invalid
in first degree (as defined for invalidity pension); Lei 10,000 for an invalid
in the second degree; or Lei 5000 for an invalid in the third degree. Free
prostheses. Free transport within home town, plus two free long-distance train
journeys per year. People who were permanently handicapped during the
revolution are also entitled to a pension.
Benefits for Other Individuals
Eliaibilitv rules and benefit levels: elderly people are entitled to
three types of benefits: If they have no pension at all (e.g. because they
have never worked in the state sector), they are entitled to a social
assistance pension of Lei 500/month. The eligibility rules for this pension
are the same as those for the social assistance cash benefits for the
handicapped, i.e. the pensioner must be too infirm to work, and must have no
relatives with a wage in excess of Lei 1000/month/person. If an elderly
person has no or only a very small income, they are eligible for free
residential care. If an elderly person has no or only a very small income,
they are eligible for two free meals a day at a social assistance canteen.
Non-elderly people are also entitled to free residential care and free meals
on the same terms as elderly people. Caseworkers are also empowered to help
fami'.ies in other ways e.g. finding a job for a member of the applicant's
family, placing children into institutional care or one-time cash payments to
meet with exceptional needs. The law at present makes no provision for cash
payments on a regular basis to anyone other than the elderly or handicapped
individuals.
Duration of benefit: in principle no limit.
Administration of Social Assistance
Administration is by a team in each Primaria. Schools for social
workers were closed twenty years ago and are only just re-opening. Thus there
is a shortage of trained caseworkers, and no trained caseworkers younger than
their mid-40s.



54
Annex 1
Page 14 of 17
Decisions about eligibility are made by the social assistance team on
the basis, where relevant, of: the applicant's pension entitlement; a visit
to the applicant's home for verification of their standard of living;; and (in
the case of handicapped people) an assessment of the degree of their handicap
by a doctor specialized in such assessment.
Though the various benefits are established by law, and the system is
national in principle, there can be local variation in the detailed
application of the national norms. The system gives the caseworker
considerable discretion as to the treatment of applicants.
Reform issues
As part of social assistance reform, the MOLSP prepared a White Paper on'
Social Assistance (July 1993) which recomnends the following:
- Extend the child allowance benefit for all children.
- Provide income support to all individuals living below the poverty
line.
- Provide family cash allowance to help foster families.to care children
in their homes who might otherwise be placed in institutionalized care
as it was common in the past.
- Provide emergency benefits to individuals or families that experience
crisis situations.
- Continue to provide meals for the elderly and cash benefits for
handicapped.
- Eliminate gradually the benefits for wives of soldiers, birth
indemnities, and indemnity for mothers with three children and more.
Based on this White Paper, a draft of the new Cash Benefit Law is now
being prepared. Soon it will be submitted for the Parliament's approval.

1. Romania seeks a loan in support of an Employment and
Social Protection Project. The loan will support investments to
the following main objectives of the Project
- reduction in unemployment ;
- productivity growth ;
- assistance to the most d.3advantaged categories of
populat:,rin that are threatened by poverty during and
after trnwisition tc market economy ;
- improve efficiency and viability of employment and
social protection programs.
The main policy actions already undertaken by the GOR and
to be undertaken over the duration oi the project to insure the
project objectives are described in this Pollay Letter.



70                          Annex 3
Page 2 of 7
X. * ZWAOUC?ZOn
2.  Four years ago, Romania began the transition to a
democracy and a market economy. Much has been achieved since
then. Fundamental changes have been made in the role of the state
in the economy. Prices and wages have been liberalized, property
has been privatized, the tax system has been reformed and the tax
burden on entreprises curtailed, and actions have been taken to
develop factor markets and the institutions that support them.
All of these actions have been taken in the face of a steadily
worsening external environment and a sharp decline in production
and income
3.   The social costs of the transition have been high. The
fall in GDP has affected the incomes of virtually all households.
In July 1993, real wages had fallen 34,6 % since October 1990,
and registered unemployment became 9 % of the active population.
The fiscal squeeze has required a lowering of transfers from
G6vernment to households. Pension expenditures as a share of GDP
have fallen from 7,2 % in 1990 la 6,4 % in 1992, and the average
real pension in the main state scheme covering 72 % of pensioners
has fallen 37,2 % over the same period.
4.   The GOR  considers  an effective  system of  social
protection to be an essential part of the transition program. In
the face of increasing needs and declining resources, the GOR has
sought to increase the targeting of existing programs so as not
to waste resources, that are already limited,and to introduce
new, cost-efective programs to meet new needs. Since 1990, the
Government has taken the following steps :
(a)  to assist those unemployed by the restructuring,
an unemployment fund was created in 1991, which
provides  benefits  and  supports  pro-active
employment programs (i.e. training and retraining
of the unemployed, etc.) ;
(b)  to improve the efficiency of administration of
short-term  benefits   (mainly  the  temporary
disability   leave)   and  reduce  fraud,   the
responsability of the first ten days of sick
leave was transfered from the social insurance to
the firm in April, 1992 ;
(c)  to   assist   those   negatively   affected   by
transition, increased funding was provided for
community social assistance programs such as
social canteens and occasional benefits ;



71
Annex 3
Page 3 of 7
(d) to strengthen and improve the targeting of
support for families with children, a single,
universal child allowance payment, covering all
children in Romania was introduced, replacing the
previous system of payments and credits, which
had covered only certain categories of childxen
and had also provided for 20 % reduction in the
income tax to people with children ; two million
more children are thus covered now, at a lower
cost ;
(e) to reduce institutionalization of children under
special circumstances, a number of policies
initiatives have been taken including a foster
familly allowance which supplements the child
allowance ;
(f) to improve responsiveness and flexibility of the
social assistance system, decentralization of
administration has begun.
During the process of loan preparation, the GOR agreed
with the World Bank on a number of additional policy actions ao
support the objectives of the project. These are d.iascribed below.
U * UWLOTDT am TRAZEIN
5.  In addition to the unemployment benefit mentioned
above  (para.4(a)), the Government. as part of it.;
program approved by Parliament in March 1993, aims to
improve employment and training opportunities by the
following policy measures :
(a)  retrainimg adults in order to be reintegrated
into the work force ;
(b)  training  y:.ng  men  and  women  for  jobs  or
professiort% in demand on labour market ;
(c)  improving professional training in accordance
with the highest technological level, with modera
methods of organization and administration.
6.   Since the actions needed to implement these policy
measures in the proposed project do not require any additional
legislation, the Government has already taken these actions. For

example, in accordance with the Government policy of promoting
cooperation among the social partners, a tri-partite National
Training Board, which aims to improve the responsiveness of
training to the rapidly evolving labour market, has been
established with representation from private and public
employers, workers' representatives and Government ministries.
Likewise, a protocol has been signed between the Ministry of
Labour and Social Protection and the Kinistry of Education to
improve occupational counseling and information to be made
available to students and workers through the project. These two

employers

Mmocil al iut-
7.   The GOR has reformed the social assistance system to
improve targeting by providing a means-tested cash benefit that
will bring the poor famillies to a minimum guaranteed income
level. Towards this goal, the following activities have been
completed :
(a) A White Paper on Social Assistance was prepared
by a team from the Direction of Social Assistance
and was published in Romania in June, 1993. The
White Paper reviews Romania's present system of
social assistance, makes a critical assessment of
it and proposes one that suits the needs of the
transition to a market economy.Tihe recomended
option provided a system of integrated cash
benefits aimed at alleviating poverty that is
financially viable in Romania. This would be
complemented by community      based    social
services   aimed  at  helping   famillies   and
individuals in crisis. The White Paper was widely
distributed in the media, other agencies and the
general public. Newspaper articles, television
and radio programs have mentioned the White Paper
and a broad debate has been initiated on the
policy issues raised in the paper. The White
Paper was discussed with staff of district social
assistance offices in June, 1993.



7 3               \         Annex 3
Page 5 of 7
(b)  A draft creating the new cash benefit will be
completed and will be submitted to Parliament for
approval, in November 1993. The Law would
abrogate untargeted benefits and proposes a
means-tested cash benefit aimed st famillies
under a minimum income level, as mentioned in
paragraph 7 (b). Determination of eligibility
will depend on the household income based on
income certificates and asset test and a set-
aside wage will be included so to encourage
working of social assistance beneficiaries.
Roughly 10 % of households are expected to be
eligible for the new cash benefit, and the system
is expected to cost about 1 % of GDP annually in
recurrent costs.
(c) A plan to implement the new cash benefit system
will be developed
Social Security Reform
8.   In 1989, Romania's social security system contained
over ten different funds. Contribution rates differed
by sector, benefits by occupation, with no portability
between  funds.  The  structure  of  benefits  was
inequitable, administration inefficient, and the whole
system unaf fordable. The Government's initial reaction
to the needs to shed labour in state entreprises was
to lower the already low retirement age. This influx
of retirees, combined with the collapse of the
revenues to the agricultural pension system during the
land reform period, provoked a system crisis. Initial
steps were taken in 1991-1992 to improve the
systems'cash flow position and safeguard reserves,
reduce administrative duplication and improve the
equity of the system. At the same time, the GOR agreed
to prepare a comprehensive reform program, using funds
from the TA/Critical Imports Loan to contract foreign
expertize as needed.
9.   This reform is now being prepared. By the end of
October 1993,the GOR willhave issued its White Paper on Social
Insurance, detailing the current situation and the reforms to be
undertaken to create a financially sustainable, equitable,
efficient system of public social  insurance which provides
adequate income security and, in doing so, effectively prevented
poverty, especially among the elderly.
10. The proposed reform includes eight actions, to be
implemented over the period 1994-1997



Annex .3
Page 6 of 7
(a)   tif ication - Romania will have "one, mandatory
public system with an integrated administration
and full portability of benefits across sectors
and occupations ;
(b)  XquLtable Rienfit structure - there will be a
minimum social benef it, and all other benefits
will be based on contributions in an equitable
manner. To achieve this goal, the retirement age
increased and equalized between men and women, as
will retirement ages across sectors with the
exception of roughly 10-15 % of the labour force
working in exceptionally arduous conditions ;
(C)  Znczased incentives for  1abou  paticipation -
once the standard retirement age and years of
pension have been reached, pensions will increase
by about 1,5-2 % per year of service to increase
incentives to continue working and contributing;
(d)  Coaplamentary  prlvat,  pnsions  - options  to
introduce  the  regulatory  and  institutional
structure for a system of private pensions,
complementary to the public system, will be
considered ;
(e)  zndfxatiou  of bnefits, *eazixae to calculate
pension  bass  - to  reduce  uncertainty,  thus
improving the microeconomic  efficiency of the
system,   formal  rules  guaranteeing  partial
indexation of pensions to price changes and
indexing earnings for pension baLse calculation to
the average wage will be adopted. The number of
base years for pension calculation will gradually
be extended to improve equity ;
(f) Fiancina  -  to  increase   transparency,  all
contributions will be re-assessed on both
employers and employees in the state sector
equally. The special tax on agro-enterprises
earnmarked for pension benefits will be
abrogated. Transparency will also be increased
by transferring the financing of all non-
insurance benefits to the state budget. To
promote the development of pension systems and
increase the targeting of the public system, a
ceiling on contributions (employees only) and
benefits will be introduced.

(g) Coasistent tax treatuent - parallel to the
introduction of the global income tax, a
consistent tax treatment for contributions and
payments, which discourages fraud and improves
equity, will be introduced. The option of making
payments taxable and contributions tax-exempt is
being considered ;
(h) a&ninistration - through the creation of an
independent agency, contribution and benefit
administration will be streamlined to improve
client service, reduce the administrative burden
on the firm, and incease efficiency.
11.  By October  1993,  the GOR will have developed a
coherent and comprehensive legislative strategy, based
on the proposals included in the White Paper on Social
Insurance. By the end of 1993, the draft law on the
new system of Social Insurance will have been
submitted to Parliament.

SOCIAL ASSISTANCE WHITE PAPER
This report describes the current social assistance system in Romania,
focusing on cash benefits, in-kind assistance and the role of the Ministry of
Labor and Social Protection, the primary government agency responsible for
social assistance. The report identifies major weaknesses of the existing
system and presents the rationale for changing the existing structure of
social assistance benefits in Romania. Several options are assessed and
recounendations are made on how to restructure the system of income suppert
and social services to better meet the needs of households that are
experiencing severe difficulties from unemployment, poverty and the social
dislocation that have developed from the establishment of a market economy.
Section I of the report describes the existing system of social
assistance in Romania. The assistance includes a range of specific cash
benefits, in-kind services and selected tax exemptions, and subsidiew for
certain categories of vulnerable individuals in specified situations as well
as institutional care for children and adults. These existing cash benefits to
families and individuals under a variety of prescribed circumstances include:
state children's allowance, benefits for mothers of three or more children,
birth indemnity, support allowance after unemployment insurance has run out,
benefit for military wives, occasional benefits for pensioners, death
allowance,and quarterly payments for individuals unable to work.
The Ministry of Labor and Social Protection (MOLSP) provides a variety
of social assistance and social insurance benefits to children and families,
the unemployed, the handicapped and pensioners. Many other ministries and
agencies at the central level of government also have responsibility for the
provision of the social assistance programs. Others include the State
Secretariat for the Randicapped, the Ministry of Education and Science, the
Ministry of Health, the Ministry of Justice, the Central Commission for the
Protection of Minors (within MOLSP), the Romanian Committee for Adoptions, the
Inter-Ministerial Committee for the Coordination of Humanitarian Programs for
Romania, and the Support Committee for Child Protection institutions.
In addition, a,: he local level, the county councils, the Mayor's
Offices and Tutelary Authorities have certain respornsibilities in the
provision of these social assistance programs.
Although the goals of the social asuistance system have changed since
1989, the legal framework, organization, and financing of benefits and
supports have remained relatively unchanged from the previous period. Prior to
1989 the objectives of social assistance were:
- -   To increase the numbers of births and ultimately the size of the
workforce;
--    To provide a minimum level of care to former workers (pensioners
and the elderly) and sick persons;



78
Annex 4
Page 2 of 7
- -    To provide a minimal level of sustenance for persons who were
judged to be incapable of working due to invalidity; and
- -    To provide institutional care for chronically ill and handicapped
adults and sick, handicapped or abazdoned children.
The goals of the social assistance system that are now evolving are:
- -    To reestablish the family am a primary focus of social welfare
policy. This orientation reflects a return to the belief in the
family's role as the most important unit for raising children and
fostering societal values.
--    To assure that all members of the society have the financial,
health, educational, and social resources to have at least a
minimally adequate standard of living. The Romanian Constitution,
articles 43-46, states that the government has the responsibility
to ensure an adequate standard of living for each person in the
society.
- -    To promote the raising of children within a child's biological
family. When families are experiencing difficulties, whenever
feasible, the child should be supported within the family rather
than placed in an institution. When a family is experiencing
difficulties, efforts would be focused on helping the family
rather then removing the child.
Section II of the report identifies major deficiencies of the current
social assistance system and concludes that change is necessary. First, many
vulnerable, at risk individuals and families are not eligible for the
assistance they need. These include individuals who are not working in public
enterprises and individuals who do not receive benefits to which they are
entitled because current budget allocations have been exhausted. Still others
receive intermittent assistance that provides income below a minimum standard.
Second, the current system wastes public funding. Public expenditures
are inappropriately exhausted through excessive reliance on iznstitutional
placement of children, and to a lesser extent the elderly despite the fact
that institutional care is the most costly means of intervention. In addition.
government resources for social assistance are not used in ways that maximize
their impact. For example, current cash benefits are not targeted on
individuals and families in the greatest need.
And third, government funding promotes policies that no longer reflect
societal goals. A large share of the government's social assistance cash
benefits, for example, continues to be used to encourage large familiea.
Similarly, a major share of government'a social assistance resources are used
to maintain children in institutions rather than to reinforce familiea'
ability to care for their children at home using community-baxed assistance.
These problems have created widespread support within Romania to reform



79
Annex 4
Page 3 of 7
the social assistance system. The goal of reform is to create the legal,
administrative and organizational framework, as well as the operational
mechbanims, to meet the economic and social needs of all households living in
poverty. The reforms are both to provide assistance which is not currently
provided by other components of the social protection system and to utilize
society's resources more effectively.
Options for Reform of Cash Benefits
Section III presents three options to reform the cash benefit prog.cams
in Romania. These are:
1)    Continuation of the existina. untaraeted cateaorical benefit structure
This option would leave the current system unchanged. Maintaining the
current social assistance system is not recosmended because it would leave the
major problem  identified in section 11 unchanged with potentially dire social
consequences for Romania. Problems of extreme poverty and the resulting social
decay and societal instability would be unaddressed at the sane time t2iat
limited government resources were not used optimally. This approach would
perpetuate a system in which there is a rapidly growing unmet need for
assistance while precious resources are wasted.
2)    Add a cas  benefit f   the poor to the existinc. cateaorical benefits
This approach would retain the existing, categorical benefit structure
but would add a new  enef it targeted on the poor. This option is judged to be
undesirable because it too would leave many of the major problems of the
existing system unchanged. Further, this option creates two additional
problems making it an infeasible choice. First, there would be one more
benefit program to administer with a separate administrative structure. .iis
would be costly and duplicative. And more important, thet addition of the.
benefit program for the poor would add additional costs to the social
assistance system without producing any savings from the consolidation of
untargeted programs.
3)    Consolidate many of the existina  categorical benefits and establ1
benefit taraeted on the poor
Such a reform would include two major components:
- -    Income support: to provide a minimum guaranteed income, below
which a household would be living in poverty; and to cons. .1ate
and eliminate several of the existing categorical benefit programs
to target and improve assistance.
Social services: to assist a person or family who cannot carry out
basic functions because of a crisis, overwhelming difficulties or
other severe problems.



80
Annex 4
Page 4 of 7
This approach would remedy the major problem. of the existing system
while beginning to addr s the emrging national social policy directions. A
minimum income standard would be set that is both socially acceptable and
fiscally feasible. Households would be entitled to receive this level of
finacial assistance which might vary in different geographical regions,
depending on the local conditions and available resources. Receipt of cash
benefits would be linked to an expanded program to enable individuals who can
work to be trained for the work force and to find employment.
The social service component would develop a comuunity-based network of
social services to assist families when they are beginning to experience
difficulties. Such an approach would reduce the need for out of home
placements of children, strengthen families, ability to function and contain
government expenditures for institutional placements.
Xt is recommended that the most feasible course for Romania to pursue at
this time is option 3--the creation of a social assistance systea that is
targeted to provide financial assistance to the poor and social sorvices and
other supports to households experiencing difficulties. Thlis approach should
begin as a series of pilot projects to test its feasibility and determine its
cost. It should then be modified as needed and phased in across the country.
It is proposed that a new social assistance system be created by
retaining certain benefits; eliminating those benefits which are either
untargeted, inefficient or not focused on current policy goals; consolidating
other benefits for ease of administration and efficiency; and adding a new
benefit for households living in poverty. It is proposed that the new social
assistance system include the following cash and in-kind benefits.
1.    A Children's Allowance granted to All ChlIdren. This benefit would
be provided to all families for each child under the age of 19.
The benefit recognizes that all families need assistance in caring
for their children, regardless of their income. The benefit
expresses the society's support for the institution of the family.
2)    Income Support to Assist All Individuals Living Below the Poverty
Line. These benefits would be provided until the person is able to
secure enough income through work to no longer l$ive below the
poverty line. The benefit should ensure that the person or family
will have a sufficient income to live at or above the poverty line
and have at least a minimum standard of living.
3)    Poster Family Cash Allowance. This benefit would help foster
families care for children in their homes who might otherwise need
to be placed in an institution.
4)    Occasional Cash lef gits for Inividuals and Families- These
benefits would assist individuals and families who experience a
crisis or an emergency situation which they could not handle with
their resources alone. In many but not all of these situations a



Annex4
Page 5 of 7
child or other individual would be at risk of abandonment,
homelessness, or out-of-home placement (institutionalization or
family foster care).
5)   Koals for the Elderly. The frail elderly who are unable to leave
their homes would be entitled to have meals delivered to their
home. Canteens would provide food to the elderly who can get to
the canteen regularly. People will pay for the food on a sliding
scale.
6)    Cash benefits for the handicapped. These benefits would provide
financial assistance to the handicapped and their families to help
them better handle the special needs of these individuals.
Handicapped individuals who are not receiving a disability pnsimOL
would be eligible to receive the benefit.
7)    Denefits for Wives of Soldiers. Theme benefits would continue but
would not be indexed to the cost of living. Eventually the income
support cash benefit would provide the primary help to soldiers
wives in need of financial assistance.
8)    Birth Zndemnity. This benefit would continue but would not be
indexed to the cost of living. Eventually it would be a less
significant benefit to families.
The means-tested social assistance benefit for the unemployed that is
currently pro-ided after unemployment benefits run out would be consolidated
into the new income support cash benefit for families living below a poverty
level. That is, when unemployment benefits run out, families will be eligible
to receive the income support for families in poverty.
Administrative Structure to Deliver tht Income Support
and Cash Benefit ProQrams
There are three principal options for the administration of the new
program: 1) continue to use the current administrative structure, 2) use
separate administration for each categorical program, and 3) develop an
integrated benefits program with decentralized eligibility determination and
centralized administration and distribution. Each of these options is assessed
in the Report and Option 3 is recommended.
Under this option, individuals are certified for most social assistance
benefits in the same decentralized community-based office, most likely the
Mayor' s Office. Cash benefit payments however are administered centrally
(either through the local Directorate of Social Assistance or by the central
Ministry of Labor and Social Protection).
Given the limited resources available and the availability of existing
administrative structures  the most feasible approach for administering the



92
Page 6 of 7
new cash benefit programs in Romania appears to be Option 3, to decentralize
eligibility dete-  nations to local commnuities by relying on existing
adAmniutrative st ucture. This would entail decentralizing eligibility
determinations to the mayors' offices in local towns and cities. They would be
the primary point of contact for families seeking cash benefits, including the
state childrens allowance, the Income Support for Families in Poverty, the
Occasional Benefits, the Birth IndAmnity and Foster Family Payments. The
Tutelary Authorities witbin the mayors offices would conduct the social
inquiries where necessary. The data gathered or recotmmendations for benefits
made by the mayors' offices would be forwarded to the Directorate of Social
Assistance of the Ministry of Labor and Social Protection for review and a
final determination.1  Payments to families could be made by the Directorate
of Social Assistance of the Ministry or centrally by the Ministry of Labor end
Social Protection.
This approach has the advantage of providing local decision-making for
benefits, with review and oversight by the Ministry of Labor and Social
Protection. The approach would like convenient for clients who would have one
location within their community in which all cash benefits would be available.
Fundina the New System
Funding for the cash benefit program for the poor would be from the
national government because issues related to poverty are a national
responsibility, requiring national remedies. Funding might come from three
principal sources: fundA from existing benefit programs that wculd be
eliminated or consolidated, the elimination of tax exmptions, and funds that
would have to be allocated.
In 1992 94.5 billion lei were spent on tax credits for families with
children. This represents 1.6 percent of Romania' s Gross Domestic Product in
1992 of 5.8 trillion lei.
Based on the 1992 e;penditure level for programs that would be
eliminated, it is estimated that the savings from the consolidation or
elimination of current programs would be 8.4 billion lei, about 0.14 percent
of GDP.
Estimates of the cost of the cash benefit programs would have to be
developed before determining the amount of new funding that would have to be
allocated for the program.
Option for Reform of Social Services
1 This is true except for Occasional Benefits for which final decisions
and payments will be made by the Mayor's Office.

Page 7 of 7
The second major reform that is proposed iu to provide social services
to households experiencing severe difficulties or crises. Emergency social
assistance is needed for families during periods of crisis when children or
other members of the household are at risk of harm or abandonment.
One option to provide needed services would create cauimity-based
wilti-service centers in which eligibility for services would be conducted and
needed services would be available. Although this option is discussed, further
research and elaboration will be needed to determine if such an approach is
appropriate to implement in Romania at this time, given the country's
resources and level of need.
This approach would establish in local communities a multi-service
center in which eligibility would be established for available social
services, and some services themselves might be available. Such centers would
assist families during the normal course of their lives as well as during
crises. These centers are referred to as locations for "one stop shopping for
services. 
The social service program could provide, depending on the family's
needs: assistance in caring for a new born, alcohol and substance abuse
programs, domestic violence programs, parent aids and parent training,
teaching parents skills to cope with their problems, day care, advocacy on
behalf of the client, help with finding housing, information on available
services, and referring the families to other agencies (for example, the
unemployment office, health services, or the mayor's office.)
The elderly are also a group who need the assistance of community-based
social service centers. One option is for the MOLSP to develop a program which
could provide community-based supports for elderly people who are at risk of
harm in their homes or are at risk of being institutionalized. These support
centers might be associated with, or separate from, the community-based family
support centers.
Next St=D
Moving forward with proposed changes to the social assistance system
will require establishing the eligibility criteria; determining the poverty
threshold and benefit levels; working out the necessary legal, organizational,
and administrative framework to create the cash benefit program; enacting the
needed legislative changes and establishing a phased implementation plan which
specifies how existing programs would be phased out as the new benefit is
phased in and how the program will be administratively established across the
country.
The next step on the proposal for a network of social service supports
include review of alternative program models, a study of the feasibility of
implementing a social service program in Romania at this time, and pilot
testing of one or several models in various parts of the country.
